    actionType: 'config_update_organisation_config',
    description: 'Apply a single dot-path patch to the organisation\'s operational_config_override JSONB. Writes config_history with change_source=config_agent. Sensitive paths route through review queue.',
    actionCategory: 'worker',
    topics: ['clientpulse', 'config', 'agent'],
    isExternal: false,
    readPath: 'none',
    defaultGateLevel: 'review',
    createsBoardTask: false,
    payloadFields: ['path', 'value', 'reason', 'sourceSession'],
    parameterSchema: z.object({
      path: z.string().describe('dot-path into operational_config (e.g. alertLimits.notificationThreshold)'),
      value: z.unknown().describe('JSON-serialisable new value'),
      reason: z.string().describe('Operator rationale (logged)'),
      sourceSession: z.string().optional().describe('Chat session id (optional)'),
    }),
    retryPolicy: {
      maxRetries: 2,
      strategy: 'fixed',
      retryOn: ['db_error'],
      doNotRetryOn: ['validation_error', 'drift_detected'],
    },
    mcp: { annotations: { readOnlyHint: false, destructiveHint: false, idempotentHint: true, openWorldHint: false } },
    idempotencyStrategy: 'keyed_write',
  },
  notify_operator: {
    actionType: 'notify_operator',
    description: 'Internal operator-facing alert â€” writes a notification row + (on approval) fans out to configured channels (in-app, email, slack).',
    actionCategory: 'worker',
    topics: ['clientpulse', 'intervention', 'alert'],
    isExternal: false,
    readPath: 'none',
    defaultGateLevel: 'review',
    createsBoardTask: false,
    payloadFields: ['title', 'message', 'severity', 'recipients', 'channels'],
    parameterSchema: z.object({
      title: z.string().describe('Alert title'),
      message: z.string().describe('Alert body'),
      severity: z.enum(['info', 'warn', 'urgent']).optional(),
      recipients: z.object({
        kind: z.enum(['preset', 'custom']),
        value: z.union([z.string(), z.array(z.string())]),
      }).describe('Preset recipient group or explicit user ID list'),
      channels: z.array(z.enum(['in_app', 'email', 'slack'])).min(1).describe('Channels to fan out to'),
    }),
    retryPolicy: {
      maxRetries: 1,
      strategy: 'fixed',
      retryOn: ['db_error'],
      doNotRetryOn: [],
    },
    mcp: { annotations: { readOnlyHint: false, destructiveHint: false, idempotentHint: false, openWorldHint: false } },
    idempotencyStrategy: 'keyed_write',
  },
};

/**
 * Legacy action-slug aliases.
 *
 * Per contract (l) in tasks/builds/clientpulse/session-1-foundation-spec.md
 * Â§1.3: all inbound action-slug surfaces MUST normalise via `resolveActionSlug`.
 * Routes, webhook handlers, queue consumers, anything that receives an
 * `action_type` from an external caller.
 *
 * The migration in `0181_rename_operator_alert.sql` rewrites historical rows,
 * but in-flight job payloads, cached definitions, dashboard filters, and
 * external callers may still carry the pre-Session-1 slug. Resolving via this
 * map is defence in depth â€” once per process per alias hit is logged so drift
 * is visible without swamping the log.
 *
 * Append-only: entries can be added but never silently removed. Removal
 * requires a deliberate code change.
 */
export const ACTION_SLUG_ALIASES: Readonly<Record<string, string>> = Object.freeze({
  'clientpulse.operator_alert': 'notify_operator',
  config_update_hierarchy_template: 'config_update_organisation_config',
});

const loggedAliasHits = new Set<string>();

/**
 * Normalise an inbound action-type slug to its canonical registered form.
 *
 * Returns the canonical slug if the input matches an alias; returns the input
 * unchanged otherwise. First hit per alias per process logs a warning so alias
 * consumption is observable without log spam.
 */
export function resolveActionSlug(slug: string): string {
  const canonical = ACTION_SLUG_ALIASES[slug];
  if (canonical === undefined) return slug;
  if (!loggedAliasHits.has(slug)) {
    loggedAliasHits.add(slug);
    // eslint-disable-next-line no-console
    console.warn(
      `[action-registry] legacy slug consumed: '${slug}' â†’ '${canonical}'. Update the caller.`,
    );
  }
  return canonical;
}

/**
 * Test-only â€” reset the log-once set so tests can assert the first-hit log
 * fires exactly once per alias per process. Never call from production code.
 */
export function __resetActionSlugAliasLogOnceForTests(): void {
  loggedAliasHits.clear();
}

/** Check if an action type is known. Routes through the alias resolver. */
export function getActionDefinition(actionType: string): ActionDefinition | undefined {
  return ACTION_REGISTRY[resolveActionSlug(actionType)];
}

/**
 * Sprint 5 P4.1 â€” returns the action types of all universal skills.
 * Re-exports from the dependency-free universalSkills.ts so callers
 * that already import from actionRegistry don't need to change.
 */
import { UNIVERSAL_SKILL_NAMES } from './universalSkills.js';
export { UNIVERSAL_SKILL_NAMES };
export function getUniversalSkillNames(): string[] {
  return [...UNIVERSAL_SKILL_NAMES];
}

/** Valid action statuses for state machine enforcement */
export const VALID_ACTION_STATUSES = [
  'proposed', 'pending_approval', 'approved', 'executing',
  'completed', 'failed', 'rejected', 'blocked', 'skipped',
] as const;

export type ActionStatus = typeof VALID_ACTION_STATUSES[number];

/** Legal state transitions */
export const LEGAL_TRANSITIONS: Record<string, string[]> = {
  proposed: ['pending_approval', 'approved', 'blocked', 'skipped', 'failed'],
  pending_approval: ['approved', 'rejected'],
  approved: ['executing'],
  executing: ['completed', 'failed'],
  // Terminal states: completed, failed, rejected, blocked, skipped â€” no transitions out
};


codex
- §6.1 + §7.4: `normaliseIntentPure` is described as pure and “same input → same output,” but `NormalisedIntent.normalisedAt` makes the returned object clock-dependent. Fix: remove `normalisedAt` from the pure return type or stamp it outside `normaliseIntent()` in the impure service layer.

- §5 + §11.4: `validatePlanPure.ts` is declared a pure module, but §11.4 makes validation success write to `planCache` and emit `planner.classified`, which are side effects. Fix: keep `validatePlanPure` side-effect free and move cache/event writes into `crmQueryPlannerService` after successful validation.

- §6.2 + §15.2: `QueryPlan.source` and `ExecutorResult.source` include `'unsupported'`, but the committed `BriefResultSource` only allows `canonical | live | hybrid`, so the normaliser can emit an invalid wire value. Fix: keep `unsupported_query` on the error path only, or split executable plans/results from non-executable planner outcomes.

- §6.2 + §15.2: `PrimaryEntity` includes `'tags'`, but `BriefStructuredResult.entityType` does not, and §15.2 maps `entityType = plan.primaryEntity` directly. Fix: remove unsupported entity literals from `PrimaryEntity` for v1 or define an explicit entity-type mapping before result normalisation.

- §6.2 + §15.2: `QueryFilter.operator` uses internal literals like `ne`, `nin`, `starts_with`, `is_null`, and `is_not_null`, while the shared Brief contract documents a different operator vocabulary, yet §15.2 says filters are copied straight through. Fix: declare one source-of-truth operator set or add an explicit `QueryFilter -> BriefResultFilter` mapping.

- §8.3 + §11.2: Stage 1 skips Stage 4 entirely and relies on per-entry parsers, so parser-produced filters/projections can bypass field-existence, projection-overlap, and permission checks; the `parseArgs` hook is not even defined in §6.3’s registry entry type. Fix: either run Stage 1 outputs through the validator or constrain Stage 1 entries to fixed registry-authored plans and add `parseArgs` to the formal type contract.

- §9.3 + §19 P1: P1 ships Stage 2, but only Stage 3-validated plans are cacheable and the P1 Stage 3 stub never produces one, so the cache is inert and the miss-path behaviour is underspecified. Fix: either defer Stage 2 to P2, allow validated Stage 1 writes in P1, or explicitly state that the Stage 3 stub short-circuits to `unsupported_query` before validator/cache logic.

- §10.2 + §11.2 + §19 P2/P3: P2 enables Stage 3 plus hybrid validation, but P3 is when `hybridExecutor` ships, so P2 can classify a valid hybrid query with nowhere to dispatch it. Fix: make P2 downgrade all hybrid plans to `unsupported_query`, or defer hybrid classification itself until P3.

- §11.2 rule 8 + §14.1: The canonical-precedence tie-breaker silently strips live-only filters whenever `canonicalCandidateKey` is set, which can change the user’s semantics instead of preserving them as hybrid/live. Fix: only promote to canonical when no live-only filter would be dropped, otherwise keep the plan hybrid/live and fail explicitly if the pattern is unsupported.

- §15.4: The approval card uses `crm.send_email` with `actionArgs { contactIds, templatePickerRequired }`, but the registered `crm.send_email` action schema requires `from`, `toContactId`, `subject`, and `body`, so the card is not dispatchable as specified. Fix: either target an existing action that accepts batch/template selection or redefine the approval payload to match the registered action schema.

- §6.3 + §12.2 + §18.1: `requiredCapabilities` are declared on registry entries, but neither Stage 1 nor `canonicalExecutor` enforces them, and the route gate hardcodes `canonical.contacts.read`, which is wrong for revenue/opportunity queries. Fix: enforce `entry.requiredCapabilities` before dispatch and derive route permissions from the selected plan/registry entry rather than a contacts-only capability.

- §13.3 + §16.6 + §24.5: The spec says live-read safety is enforced “by convention” until a future dependency rule exists, then later claims read-only is structural and compile-time enforced, which overstates the v1 mechanism. Fix: either ship a named static import rule in v1 or downgrade every “structural/compile-error” claim to “import-discipline + code review” language.

- §9.2 + §11.11 + §5: Cache invalidation on `canonical_subaccount_mutations` version changes is load-bearing, but no listener, poller, or invalidation function is named anywhere in the file inventory or implementation sections. Fix: name the concrete invalidation mechanism/file, or cut v1 back to TTL-only invalidation.

- §6.6 + §17.1 + §17.2: The observability contract drifts because `planner.canonical_promoted` is documented but missing from `PlannerEventKind`, and `topAliasSimilarity` / `hybrid_unsupported_rate` are promised without any defined producer or derivation rule. Fix: align `PlannerEventKind` with the documented event set and either define the exact similarity/metric computations or remove those fields from v1.

- §5 + §19 P3 + §20.2 + §20.3: The file inventory says “no client changes in v1” and claims §5 lists every file, but later sections require `integration.test.ts`, `liveExecutor.test.ts`, `hybridExecutor.test.ts`, `systemPnlService.ts`, `SystemPnlPage.tsx`, and `pressure-test-results.md`. Fix: either add every referenced file to §5 and drop the “no client changes” claim, or remove those later-file commitments.

- §20.2 + §20.4: The spec commits to route-level integration/E2E-style tests, which conflicts with the locked testing posture of static gates plus pure-function unit tests only. Fix: delete the integration-test section and restate those checks as pure tests around orchestration/translation logic.

- §8.4 + §12.2 + §20.1: `registryMatcherPure.test.ts` is listed as 15 minimum cases, but §8.4 requires every alias for all 8 entries to hit and §12.2 currently defines 35 aliases before any edge cases. Fix: update §20.1 to the true minimum or shrink §8.4 to the count you actually intend to require.

- Appendix A + §§1.2, 1.3, 22: The checklist claims a deferred-items section exists, but deferred work is split across multiple sections and several items still lack an explicit BUILD / DEFER / WON’T DO verdict in one place. Fix: add a single `## Deferred Items` section that consolidates every non-v1 item with an explicit verdict.

- §16.2 + §24.6: The per-query cent ceiling is described as checking “accumulated cost so far” before Stage 3, but that value is zero before the first billable call, so it cannot satisfy the success criterion “fires before Stage 3 budget overrun” without a prediction mechanism. Fix: either define a predicted-cost precheck tied to `costPreview` or restate the guard as a post-call breaker instead of a pre-call ceiling.

- §21.3: The per-org rollout plan assumes staged onboarding after main, which conflicts with the stated pre-production posture of no live users and no staged rollout mechanics. Fix: replace §21.3 with commit-and-revert validation language for pre-production, or explicitly mark org-by-org rollout as post-launch follow-on work.
